Current Commentary

[3] A Review and Prospect of Humiliation

[Jurchen] Before the establishment of its state, it often relied on China, paying tribute and acknowledging its vassalage. At that time, the definition of [state] was not as clear as in modern times. However, Liaodong was a county under Chinese administration beginning in the Qin Dynasty. The Liaoyang of the Han Dynasty is the present-day Fengtian. The historical facts clearly demonstrate that the three northeastern provinces are the territory of the Republic of China. Who can dare to deny this? Even though the Manchus who entered China were indeed a foreign race, their political institutions, regulations, and culture were no different from those of the Han people. Only the emperor was replaced, changing the ruling class. When the Republic of China was founded, sovereign power was returned to the 400 million citizens. In the past twenty years, there have been various disputes, but these are inevitable phenomena in the revolutionary process. They cannot be used as a pretext to deny the sovereignty of the Republic of China, nor can they be considered unique stains on the Republic of China. Transitional periods in other countries have also often witnessed such scenes. For example, in France, it took ninety years from 1789 to the establishment of the republic amidst turmoil and disputes. Since the founding of the Republic of China, for twenty-two years, there have indeed been various political and social instabilities, preventing us from achieving peace and stability. Our citizens are indeed largely to blame. Those who care about us also feel regret. However, this cannot be used as a justification to secede our territory, deny our sovereignty, trample on our people, and even disregard [justice] between nations.

Japan harbors malicious intentions and deliberately plans aggression. This is almost universally known. However, because our country is busy with internal strife and unable to concentrate its efforts on national defense, Japanese imperialists have been able to act arbitrarily, engaging in fabricating false evidence and provoking wars. From the Wanbaoshan Incident to the Nakamura-Ishimoto affair, the former was instigated by Japanese financial groups ordering Korean farmers to incite unrest, while the latter involved military spies reconnoitering our country's hinterland. When unexpected events occurred, they invoked special interests to suddenly attack our Liaoning and Jilin provinces on the night of September 18. At that time, Japan presented its so-called five preconditions (mainly seeking the rights acquired through aggression), along with guarantees of life and property, and local resolutions, forcing us into a treaty of surrender. At the same time, they sharpened their swords and tightened their bows, with troops advancing and attacking Heilongjiang, and invading Jinzhou to the west. Our country vacillated between peace and war, paying lip service to resistance, allowing the enemy to grow in power and lose more territory, and the situation became increasingly unmanageable.

The local conflicts spread to the entire country, and chaos followed. The Chinese people, compelled by circumstances, adopted the most peaceful and rational means of retaliation, hoping to attract the attention of other countries. The forceful occupation of the three northeastern provinces is not a local issue, but is related to the entire survival of the Chinese nation, and has profound and close ties with all countries in the world today. Therefore, our country's adoption of "economic isolation" against Japanese imperialists is what all humanity should have done. Unexpectedly, Japan became even more fierce, bombing Shanghai and destroying Zhabei, and while our people were catching their breath, they created a puppet regime to annex the northeast. Thus, the Japanese, invoking their so-called "benevolence," under the guise of national self-determination, single-handedly established their so-called "Manchukuo" on March 1. The world knows that the puppet regime's emergence was manufactured by the Japanese army to conceal their aggressive annexation of the three northeastern provinces. They beautified their actions by saying they were "for peace in East Asia," but in reality, the three northeastern provinces were peaceful before the Japanese militarists' invasion. After the September 18 Incident and the establishment of the puppet regime, the peaceful ["Manchuria"] became a Japanese slaughterhouse, with smoke and fire everywhere, and the sound of dogs and chickens unsettling. The Japanese imperialists used force for "special interests," and the so-called "peace" was merely an unrelated excuse.

Second, there was the southward advance for "defense against communism." This statement was most appealing. Even the experienced British, while guarding against the Soviet Union's encroachment on India from the south and its eastward expansion into China, also believed that Japan truly had the intention of "anti-communism" and the "power" to "suppress communism." Therefore, for more than a year, they expressed goodwill towards Japan, helping their iron hooves to roam freely and realize their conspiracy of annexation. When the Shanhaiguan was seized, Rehe was in a state of emergency, and Tianjin and Beiping were also in imminent danger, the countries of Britain and France began to understand that Japan's true intention was not to "guard against communism" but to occupy land, and not to resist the southward advance of communist forces but to monopolize the Chinese market. They used the name of anti-communism to manipulate countries around the world and exploit psychological terror to achieve their goals of aggression. Now the truth is clear. The League of Nations resolutely denied the [puppet state] and condemned the Japanese military on February 24, and our country has been deceived all along?

There is no doubt that the sovereignty over the northeastern territory belongs to us. The moral sanction of the League of Nations, with forty-two votes against one, can be said to have exhausted the "justice" of its abilities. However, this is only the [League of Nations overcoming itself] and overcoming the contradiction between advocating peace and condoning war. Can we over-hope that the League of Nations will use practical and effective methods to sanction the Japanese military's atrocities? We shouldn't entertain this illusion. Therefore, the battle of words should end, and the war of iron and blood should begin. Our country has suffered terrible disasters, so how can we continue to adhere to a policy of non-resistance or partial resistance, hoping for temporary peace that cannot be obtained? On this day of the puppet regime's anniversary, we should use an iron fist to toll the death knell of the puppet regime, launching our country's active and vigorous national struggle. Immediately and resolutely order the crusade against the puppet regime, wash away this humiliation with red blood, and scatter red blood across the northeast to recover our former homeland.

Stimson's Declaration: The United States Cooperates with the League of Nations 7

Preparing to Send Representatives to Participate in the Advisory Committee. Rumors That the Soviet Union Has Decided Not to Participate in the Advisory Committee

(Washington) U.S. Secretary of State Stimson announced this morning that the United States will cooperate with the League of Nations Advisory Committee, but at the same time stated that the current government's cooperation guarantee cannot bind President-elect Roosevelt, and Roosevelt may still change this policy, but based on the current situation, it is unlikely to change. Stimson also urged people to pay attention to the meaning of cooperation, which does not mean that the United States will join as a committee member because it is a League of Nations group. However, according to other officials of the State Department, the United States is prepared to send a representative to work with the committee if necessary. (27th Guomin News Agency Telegram)

(Geneva) According to sources from the Russian side here, the Soviet Russian government has decided not to participate in the work of the Twenty-One Advisory Committee. (28th Reuters Telegram)

Japan Plans to Change its Diplomatic Policy Towards the United States 8

Matsumoto to Replace Debuchi as Ambassador

(Beiping) Foreign News: Since Japan plans to withdraw from the League of Nations, Foreign Minister Uchida has given full consideration to its diplomatic policy towards the United States and has decided to abandon its past textbook-style diplomacy and replace it with a friendly diplomacy policy. According to those close to the Foreign Minister, the first step in changing the diplomatic policy towards the United States is to recall Ambassador Debuchi to the United States and replace him with Matsumoto. It remains to be seen whether his proposal can be realized. (28th Special Telegram)

(Paris) After failing at the League of Nations, Japanese representative Matsumoto became angry and today publicly scolded the American Associated Press reporter here, saying that the United States no longer has the demeanor of a diplomat and that Japan will regard the United States' participation in the League of Nations' proposed negotiation committee as suspicious and untrustworthy. The American people have long treated people unfairly, and even the American government is the same. The United States and the American people forgive China's mistakes and exaggerate Japan's mistakes. From the beginning of the Sino-Japanese dispute, the United States has used its power in the League of Nations to oppose Japan. If it were not for the United States' manipulation of the League of Nations, he believes the Manchuria case could have been resolved. (28th Special Telegram)

Guangdong People Plan to Write to the Siamese Emperor to Advise 9

Do Not Violate the League of Nations' Fair Claims

(Hong Kong) The people of Guangdong are extremely angry at Siam's collusion with Japan for profits and have nominated Xiao Focheng and Lin Yizhong to lead the writing of a letter to the Siamese Emperor, advising him not to violate the League of Nations' respect for the principles of justice and peace. The letter can be sent out during the day. (28th Special Telegram)

China Stops Participating in the Chicago Exhibition 10

Yesterday's Decision of the Executive Yuan 11

(Nanjing) The American Chicago Exhibition will open in June of this year. Our country collected exhibits and finished collecting them a few days ago. It also held a preliminary exhibition in Shanghai to prepare for participation in the United States and appointed Guo Pobai to go to the United States to supervise the construction of the pavilion. This matter was brought up for discussion at the Executive Yuan meeting on the 28th. After a long discussion, it was decided to stop participating due to financial difficulties and the deepening national crisis. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce will send polite telegrams to the United States to state the reasons. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce has urgently telegraphed the Shanghai Preparatory Committee on the 28th to handle the closing. (28th Special Telegram)

Impact of British Arms Embargo 12

Our Government Believes It Will Increase Japanese Aggression

US Action to Be Decided After Roosevelt Takes Office

Simon Says Sanctions Against Japan Must Be Carefully Considered

(Nanjing) A notification from Britain regarding the ban on arms exports to both China and Japan has been received here. Opinions on this matter vary widely. The Chinese authorities believe that while Britain's intention to prevent the expansion of conflict and avoid bloodshed by banning arms exports is understandable, this step will not maintain peace but will instead increase Japan's power of aggression against China. This is because the Japanese are very well equipped with weapons, while China can be said to have virtually no modern weapons. If arms sales to China are prohibited, China will have no means to resist Japanese attacks. Moreover, Japan has anticipated this move and can now purchase arms from Siam, which is not subject to the embargo. Therefore, to maintain peace, countries should seek international coordination and only implement arms export bans against aggressors. (Reuters, 28th)

(London) When Foreign Secretary Simon announced the ban on arms shipments to the Far East in the House of Commons yesterday, he mentioned the 1931 arms embargo, which tightened previous restrictions. The order prohibits the export or shipment of the following arms to foreign ports, except for those with licenses from the Board of Trade: cannons, other artillery pieces, gun carriages, ammunition, explosives, firearms, grenades, machine guns, projectiles, mines, bombs, grenade launchers, incendiary devices, fuses, torpedoes, torpedo tubes, fire extinguishers, sights, bayonets, knives, tanks, armored vehicles, and aircraft. Parts for the aforementioned arms are also included in the ban. (Reuters, 28th)

(Beiping) Although official circles have not yet commented on the British government's decision on the arms embargo, public opinion is quite shocked, believing that it suits Japan's strategy. Japan's military equipment is extremely abundant, and its stock of military supplies is greater than China's. Moreover, China's best arsenal, the Shenyang Arsenal, has long been coveted by Japan. (Reuters, 28th) (London) The Chinese in London are dissatisfied with the British Foreign Secretary Simon's announcement of the Far East arms embargo, which includes China. They argue that the League of Nations recognizes China as innocent and accuses Japan of aggression. Now, Britain is treating China and Japan the same, which is unfair. The Chinese side is awaiting instructions from Nanjing and has not yet considered lodging a protest. The Japanese side does not wish to comment on the British Foreign Secretary's announcement. (Reuters, 28th) (Washington) No action will be taken on President Hoover's proposal to ban arms shipments to belligerent countries during this session of the House of Representatives. Today, the Democrats are obstructing any action and a solution must wait until the House convenes in the next session. (Reuters, 27th)

(Washington) Senator Borah, upon hearing of the British government's decision to ban arms exports to China and Japan, stated that he does not approve of following Britain's lead. Cooperation between Britain and the United States regarding the arms embargo to the Far East is currently being blocked by Congress. The current bill in the House only prohibits arms shipments to South America, so the US President only has the power to prohibit arms supplies to South America and Chinese rebels. The Senate recently passed a bill advocating a worldwide arms embargo, but soon decided to reconsider it, leading to its being shelved. However, the US government expresses sympathy for the British arms embargo, but fears that Congress will not act quickly and may not approve the same actions as Britain until a special spring session is convened. Some members of Congress who represent the interests of arms manufacturers may object to this embargo. (Reuters, 27th)

(London) British Foreign Secretary Simon contacted the United States regarding the arms embargo issue. The United States responded today, stating that the US authorities do not have the power to prohibit arms exports. (Reuters, 27th)

(Paris) During today's cabinet meeting, the issue of banning arms shipments to the Far East was not discussed because there were many difficult cabinet matters requiring discussion. However, the government stated that it would follow the League of Nations in all matters. (Reuters)

(Washington) Today, US Secretary of State-designate Hull met with British Ambassador Lindsay for a long time. Afterwards, he only stated that the discussion concerned a broad plan to restore trade among nations and declined to provide details. However, it is generally believed here that the two discussed not only war debts, the economy, and general diplomatic issues, but also the Manchurian issue and the ban on arms shipments to the Far East. The Democratic Party has not yet made a general decision on this issue. Only a few members of the party have advocated banning arms shipments to all countries, regardless of whether they are at war. The Republican Party generally advocates limiting the scope of the ban to belligerent countries only. Senator Borah alone argues that there should be no embargo on China and Japan, because Japan can manufacture its own, while China must rely on others for supply. An embargo would indirectly help Japan. It is expected that the new government will soon announce its position on this issue, because all countries insist that arms embargo actions must be consistent worldwide, and the US cannot remain silent. (National News Agency, 27th)

(London) It is heard that for arms previously ordered from Britain, both China and Japan will be treated equally and avoid the impact of the embargo. The 1931 arms law mentioned by British Foreign Secretary Simon in the House of Commons refers to weapons of war such as arms, ammunition, and aircraft. The government believes tonight that this embargo is a measure to cut off external problems to prevent their spread, and at the same time, to encourage other countries to follow suit. If an international agreement cannot be reached in the future, Britain will reconsider its decision. (Reuters, 27th)

Careful Consideration of Sanctions 13

(London) After British Foreign Secretary Simon announced in the House of Commons this afternoon that Britain would no longer issue licenses for arms shipments to China and Japan from today onwards, Liberal Party leader Samuel stated that British public opinion is currently very dissatisfied with the Japanese government's actions in China. This is purely in terms of the rights and wrongs of the Sino-Japanese dispute. Imposing a uniform arms embargo on both sides is more unfavorable to China than to Japan because China relies entirely on foreign arms supplies. He is certain that the British people want Britain to not provide any assistance to Japan, not only in terms of arms but also in terms of loans and credit. Economic power, coupled with the moral pressure of public opinion, will eventually bring Japan to its senses. Former Foreign Secretary Austen Chamberlain stated that his sympathy for Japan has diminished with the development of the situation. We have now reached the stage where it is certain that Japan's actions in Manchuria are in serious violation of its obligations under the League of Nations Covenant, the Paris Pact, and the Nine-Power Treaty. Japan is acting rashly and engaging in risky ventures. The consequences may be far-reaching, and the price in blood and finance will be greater than the Japanese people can foresee. The House eventually rejected the motion by Labour Party leader Lansbury to reduce external expenditure. Foreign Secretary Simon concluded the debate, referring to the issue of sanctions raised by Labour MP Cripps, saying that this matter is of utmost importance and should not be discussed without careful consideration. Those who are loudly calling for sanctions now may not be able to influence the League of Nations' decision. As for the arms embargo, the British government is acting with complete friendship towards both China and Japan. He does not believe that this move is biased towards either side. Britain cannot unilaterally take actions that discriminate between the two sides. He hopes that an international agreement on future actions can be reached soon. (Reuters, 27th)

Japan's Self-Comfort 14

(Tokyo) Japanese political circles expressed their views on the speech made by the British Foreign Secretary in the House of Commons yesterday, saying that the arms embargo is more unfavorable to China than to Japan. Although Simon's speech expressed sympathy for Japan's difficulties, his words can be seen as blaming Japan, which angered the Japanese. If the embargo were imposed on China and Japan without any bias, then this anger could be concealed. But if it is imposed on Japan, then Japan will inevitably find ways to prevent arms from reaching China. Official circles believe that the raw materials for manufacturing arms may not be prohibited, but if this is also prohibited, the consequences will be very serious and unpredictable, because Japan must take some action. (Reuters, 28th)

British and American Public Opinion 15

(London) This morning, newspapers commented on Foreign Secretary Simon's announcement in the House of Commons last night of a ban on arms exports to the Far East. Some praised it as cautious, while others criticized it frankly. Except for The Times, all said that Britain's unilateral ban would be ineffective. The Times warmly praised the British government for taking this emergency action swiftly, and believed that public opinion would approve of it. Some said that the uniform ban on China and Japan was unfair to China. It should be known that Foreign Secretary Simon's theory that a single country should not favor one side over the other in a dispute is justified. Moreover, arms shipped to China are likely to fall into the hands of the Japanese, so a uniform ban is appropriate in practice. The most prudent course of action at present is only to prohibit British arms from being shipped to the Far East, so as not to implicate Britain. The second step is to reach an agreement with other arms-manufacturing countries, especially the United States, to either change or cancel today's policy, or suspend its implementation. If countries can follow Britain's lead and work together to achieve effective arms limitation in peacetime, the hope of a country waging an unlimited and prolonged war will be even more remote. However, further consideration should be given to ensuring that this approach will not be applied to countries that are invaded in the future, so as not to violate justice. The Morning Post believes that this embargo will be ineffective and merely a costly gesture. The Daily Telegraph said that a single country taking this action has nothing to do with war. As for the hope of an international agreement, it is even more remote than Simon admitted. The Daily News cautiously welcomed the decision, but said that it should not be merely a gesture and should be quickly replaced by a larger and more stringent plan, and that if Britain acts alone, it may be difficult to distinguish between China and Japan in the future. Only supporting international condemnation of Japan and international action can avoid this. The Daily Mail said that the embargo is extremely foolish, and its only foreseeable result is to increase unemployment in Britain. The Labour Party's organ, the Daily Herald, attacked Simon's statement that Britain could not take sides in the dispute, saying that while this statement is obvious in words, Japan will see it as Britain not endorsing the implementation of the covenant to resist Japan. This is exactly the assurance that the Japanese military wants to continue to obtain. (Reuters, 28th)

(Washington) The Washington Daily News editorial advocated that the world should ban the export of arms to Japan as an act of self-respect. The newspaper also stated that Americans' refusal to buy Japanese goods is already foreseeable, because many far-sighted Washington merchants have stopped importing Japanese goods. The New York Herald Tribune editorial stated that Matsuoka's speech in the League of Nations, claiming that Manchuria was obtained by Japan from Soviet Russia and that Manchuria's development was due to Japan's management, contradicts the theory that [Manchukuo] is a natural product. Armed occupation of Manchuria is naturally not an act of self-defense. Recognizing [Manchukuo] would violate Articles 1 and 2 of the Washington Five-Power Treaty. The New York Times editorial stated that Stimson's reply to the nation contained a notification to Japan, and that the new Secretary of State Hull will continue its inherent policy. (Central News Agency, 28th)

Japanese Barracks Open to Reservists

Situation at Jiukou Suddenly Becomes Tense

(Tokyo) Japanese residents in Qinhuangdao have now completely evacuated. (Central News Agency, 28th)

(Beiping) Yesterday, enemy troops on the east bank of the Shi River again attempted to repair the Shi River Bridge, but were repelled by our sentries with machine-gun fire. More than 200 reservists from the Japanese barracks in Qin Island have arrived, and the situation in Qinbu is critical. Since last night, the situation has suddenly become tense. It is heard that the Japanese side plans to attack our positions on March 1. (Japanese-Chinese Joint News Agency, 28th)

A state of extreme alert has begun day and night. According to foreign observers, the Japanese army will begin military action against North China at the end of this week. (Japanese-Chinese Joint News Agency, 28th)

Situation at Shi River Frontline Near Linyu is Quite Urgent in Recent Days 17

On the 26th and 27th, many Japanese merchant ships unloaded provisions, ammunition, and military supplies at Qinhuangdao. They also carried five or six covert squads, resembling Koreans, who landed and secretly went to the Japanese barracks. It is also rumored that Japan has a conspiracy to riot in Qinhuangdao, Tanggu, Dagu, Tianjin, Shanghai, Hankou, and other places in the coming days. On the 27th, the enemy troops at Shanhaiguan conducted a live-fire artillery exercise as a demonstration and notified merchants and civilians not to be alarmed. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

Shenyang Vehicles Almost Entirely Requisitioned 18

Japanese and Puppet Troops Issue Mobilization Order, Forcing Vagrants into the Army

(Beiping) A person from Shenyang said that more than 5,000 Japanese troops have been transferred from Sujiatun. All private and commercial heavy trucks in Shenyang have been seized by the Japanese army for use in Tongliao to prepare for the attack on Rehe. All large carts and horses owned by civilians have also been requisitioned to be used for mounting artillery. The Japanese and puppet troops issued a mobilization order on the 16th of this month, planning for the puppet troops to be the vanguard during combat, with the Japanese army supervising from behind. This kind of oppressive measure is truly deeply regrettable. (Special Dispatch, 28th) (Beiping) The Japanese and puppet army general headquarters for the Rehe campaign is located in the puppet capital of Changchun. The Japanese army is forcibly requisitioning large carts from various counties, and about 10,000 vehicles that have gone to the front lines. The Japanese army is arresting unemployed vagrants everywhere, forcing them to go to the front lines to fight. The Japanese army's plan to attack Rehe is to attack with a force of ten divisions. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) The pseudo-police in various counties of western Liaoning, acting on the orders of the Japanese army, are collecting 500 large carts in each county, requiring them to be delivered by the end of this month and concentrated in Jinzhou. The pseudo-police are urging the collection in various counties very urgently. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

Tang Yulin's Resolute Statement 19

Will Not Allow the Japanese to Acquire Rehe Until the Chinese Are All Dead

Chairman Tang Yulin of Chengde recently told Associated Press reporter E. Kingsbury that the Japanese will not be allowed to acquire Rehe until the Chinese are all dead. The current retreat to new defense lines on the front lines is all part of a planned defense strategy and is purely for tactical convenience. He expects further retreats to come, with the aim of fully defending the mountains, staying away from the railway, shortening our army's transportation and facilitating the transportation of supplies. The current battleground may be in Chifeng and Lingyuan, which are the keys to Chengde. At this time, there are expressions of resolute resistance everywhere in China. Camel teams transporting bullets and food at Gubeikou and other places are seen all the way, one after another, to reach Chengde. Camel teams also depart from Chengde to transport bullets and food to the most forward volunteer army almost every hour. Although the Chinese army and volunteer army do not have plans to defend Kailu and Chaoyang for a long time, they are still fighting the Japanese army extremely bravely. The Japanese and traitorous troops have suffered many casualties, while the Chinese side has suffered a total of 500 casualties to date, most of them on the Kailu and Chaoyang front lines. (National News Agency, 28th)

Many Japanese Soldiers Suffered Frostbite in Rehe

Japanese Encounter Main Force Resistance on Suiling Avenue

(Tokyo) The Japanese army has encountered the main force resistance on the Suizhong-Lingyuan Avenue. It is said that the Chinese army's front line is 40 miles long, and the trenches are built very firmly. However, the Hattori Brigade is still breaking through. The atmosphere is extremely cold, often 27 degrees below freezing, resulting in many cases of frostbite. (Reuters, 28th)

Our side has taken strict precautions against this poisonous scheme. (Special Dispatch, 28th) (Beiping) The Japanese authorities in Tianjin lodged a protest with Yu Xuezhong, opposing the Chinese army's deployment of defensive works in Tanggu, calling it a violation of the Boxer Protocol. The Chinese authorities have now replied, saying that Japan first violated this agreement by occupying Yuguan. If Japan does not act jointly with other signatory countries, it has no right to occupy it. Since Japan has violated the agreement first, how can it accuse China of violating the agreement? Tianjin is now like a powder keg. The Japanese are currently building various defensive structures around their concession. Chinese people point to this as a provocative act. At the same time, the Japanese consul requested Tian Xuezhong to fully protect the Japanese people in Tianjin. Yu has provided the necessary guarantees. He meant that if the Japanese army were to break through the Great Wall, the Chinese army would resist it, while assuming the responsibility of protecting the Japanese soldiers and civilians in the Japanese concession. The Chinese people are well aware that if troops are dispatched to Tianjin to protect the Japanese residents, their actions will be regarded as a provocative act, and the Japanese army will use this as an excuse to take action to implement the threats recently issued by the Japanese commander Nakamura. Danish Merchant Ship Attacked by Pirates on the Shantou-Hong Kong Route 41

First Mate Nielsen Shot 42

Bandits Land at Mos Bay 43

Three Passengers Kidnapped and Taken Back to Hong Kong by Boat 44

(Hong Kong) The American ship "Mei Xi Mei Lun" departed from Hong Kong to Shantou on the 27th and was hijacked by eight pirates, who kidnapped three passengers and injured the first mate. They sailed to Dapeng Bay, landed, and escaped, losing about 3,000 yuan in stolen goods. The pirates boarded the ship in Hong Kong. (28th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Danish ship "Gustav Ditlevsen" was en route from Hong Kong to Shantou when it encountered pirates and was taken to Dapeng Bay. It was thoroughly searched. The ship has a displacement of 135 tons and is now sailing back to Hong Kong from Dapeng Bay. (28th Reuters Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) When the pirates attacked the Danish ship "Gustav Ditlevsen", they shot the first mate Nielsen in the chest, but the injury is not dangerous. It is learned that the pirates landed at Mos Bay in English waters and did not take the ship to Dapeng Bay. The local naval authorities have taken no action on this matter because it is too late. The robbery site is only two hours away from Hong Kong. There were only eight pirates. When the attack occurred, the first mate happened to be steering the ship in place of Captain Jacobsen. The pirates rushed to the bridge. Nielsen tried to stop them and was shot. The pirates then carried Nielsen into the captain's room, and the five European crew members were also controlled and detained in the room at gunpoint. For the next hour, the ship sailed irregularly because no one was steering it. The situation was very dangerous because there was a risk of hitting a reef or running aground. Then the captain persuaded the pirate leader to allow him to steer. The pirate leader then ordered the ship to sail to Siwan. When the pirates landed, they took three Chinese passengers from the dining room and fled into Chinese territory. The ship's wireless transmitter was destroyed, but the first mate, who was the ship's radio operator, despite being shot, crawled out of the room and helped his companions repair the machine and send out a distress call. The captain called this the bravest act he had ever seen in his life. When the ship arrived in Hong Kong, it was found that Nielsen had been shot in the abdomen. Although the injury was serious, it was not dangerous. He has been sent to the hospital for treatment. (28th Reuters Dispatch)

Draft Amendment to the County Organization Law 50

Joint Review and Decision by Internal Affairs, Finance, Education, and Industry Ministries 51

(Nanjing) The draft amendment to the County Organization Law was jointly reviewed by representatives from the Internal Affairs, Finance, Education, and Industry Ministries on the 28th. The resolutions were: (1) The county is a free association and also an administrative region below the province. (2) It is determined that the county government is a preparatory agency or executive agency for county autonomy during the period of political tutelage, and also an administrative agency below the province. (3) It is determined that county affairs shall not be mixed with national or provincial affairs. (4) The provincial government shall not interfere in county affairs within the scope of not hindering central or provincial laws and regulations. (5) The county government is a complete administrative agency, and there shall be no other systematically organized organizations outside the county government. In addition, there is a chapter on county finance, which will be discussed at a meeting in three days. (28th Special Dispatch)

Resolutions of the Executive Yuan 52

Unanimous Arousal to Donate and Resist Aggression 53

Appointment of Wu Guozhen as Hubei Provincial Committee Member 54

Implementation of New Silver Coin Conversion Rate 55

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan held its 89th meeting at 9:00 a.m. on the 28th, attended by Song Ziwen, Luo Wengan, Gu Mengyu, Chen Shaokuan, Zhu Jiahua, Chen Gongbo, Shi Qingyang, Chen Shuren, and Liu Ruiheng, with Zeng Zhongming, Gan Naiguang, Chen Yi, Duan Xipeng, Zou Lin, Guo Chuntao, and Yu Feipeng present as observers. Chairman Song Ziwen made the following resolutions on important cases:

(1) President Song's proposal for the Northeast and Jehol Support Association, whose main purpose is to unite all sectors, inspire the people's patriotic heart, raise funds to support the front lines, and comfort the disaster-stricken people. It is urgent to unite the strength of the entire people and the government to be the support for defending the border and resisting aggression. It is proposed that all ministries and commissions of the Executive Yuan unanimously rise up, gather their subordinates, and donate to the best of their ability to raise funds. This will not only strengthen the determination of the soldiers at the front to fight against the enemy, but also show the spirit of unified cooperation of government personnel. The motion should be telegraphed for public decision. Resolution: Passed.

(2) Resolution to appoint Wu Guozhen as a member of the Hubei Provincial Government. (3) The Ministry of Internal Affairs reported that it had been instructed to review the County and City Council Organization Law and the date of implementation of the County and City Council Election Law, and proposed to forward them for immediate promulgation and implementation. Resolution: Passed. (4) Minister of Finance Song Ziwen proposed that the disorder of our country's currency system has long been criticized by the world. It is proposed to set the commonly used silver dollars in Shanghai and the circulating silver coins as 7 qian 1 fen 5 li of standard silver, setting a fixed conversion rate for one silver coin, and starting to implement it on March 10th of this year. It is also proposed to promulgate the Silver Standard Coin Minting Regulations, which will be minted by the Central Mint. The draft Silver Standard Coin Minting Regulations consists of 16 articles. Please make a public decision. Passed and sent to the Political Conference. (5) Minister of Finance Song Ziwen proposed that the Hunan Provincial Government should be strictly ordered to immediately abolish the additional tax on cotton yarn in order to maintain central laws and regulations and protect national treasury revenue. Passed. (28th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Constitutional Drafting Committee Decides on Research Procedure 56

(Nanjing) The Constitutional Drafting Committee has decided on a research procedure of twelve weeks. (1) February 23 to March 2: Research on territory, form of government, sovereignty, and flag colors. (2) March 2 to 9: Issues of people's rights. (3) March 9 to 16: Issues of people's obligations. (4) March 16 to 23: Issues of the National Assembly. (5) March 23 to 29: Issues of the balance of power between the central and local governments. (6) March 29 to April 5: Issues of the central government system. (7) April 5 to 13: Continued. (8) April 13 to 20: Issues of the provincial system. (9) April 20 to 27: Issues of the county system. (10) April 27 to May 4: Issues of the power to interpret the constitution and sanctions for violating the constitution. (11) May 11 to 18: Issues of the exercise of four powers, the people's livelihood, and national education. (12) May 18 to 25: Issues of the military system and national accounting. (28th Special Dispatch)

The Court Seriously Handles Zheng Yuxiu Case 57

(Nanjing) The case of impeachment of Zheng Yuxiu, Yang Zhaoyun, etc. for judicial malpractice had the evidence books of embezzled public funds sent to the Civil Service Disciplinary Committee for transfer to the Supreme Court for handling. The defendants Zheng Yuxiu, Yang Zhaosun, Zheng Huichen, etc. are all under secret arrest. (28th Special Dispatch)

Method for Abolishing Taels and Changing to Yuan 58

Two Currencies Used Simultaneously During the Trial Period 59

(Nanjing) The government has decided on a two-step method for abolishing taels and changing to yuan. March 1st will be the trial period, and the Central Mint will also start minting silver dollars at the same time. Regarding the weight and fineness of the new coins, the principle of the Coinage Regulations of the Third Year of the Republic will be followed. The Executive Yuan meeting on the morning of the 28th had a discussion on this and decided that two currencies will be used simultaneously during the trial period. Regarding the fineness issue, it has been decided that the exchange rate standard will be 7 qian 1 fen 5 li. There will be no fluctuations in the future, and the market price of silver cents will be based on this standard. In the future, the new coins will be exchanged without limit by the Central, China, and Communications Banks at standard prices. Once a large amount of new coins are minted, the abolition of taels will be implemented. (28th Special Dispatch)

Government Has Not Yet Decided to Recall Ambassador to Japan 60

Peng Xuepei Talks... 61

Actually Already in a State of Confrontation 62

No Need to Consider Severing Diplomatic Relations 63

(Nanjing) Peng Xuepei told reporters on the 28th that the diplomatic situation has been unusually urgent recently. Some advocate severing diplomatic relations with Japan or recalling the ambassador to Japan, but the government has not yet made this decision. The two sides are now facing each other with weapons and are actually in a state of confrontation. Therefore, there is no need to consider whether or not to sever diplomatic relations. The issue of minting silver coins is the first step in abolishing taels and changing to yuan. The Executive Yuan meeting has stipulated that the ratio of yuan to tael is 7.15, and this will be used as the exchange standard in the future. The mint will mint new coins with excellent patterns and colors. When they circulate in the market, the abolition of taels and the change to yuan will be even less of a problem. This case will be submitted to the Central Political Conference on March 1 for discussion. (28th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Many Incidents in Germany: Twenty Fires in Berlin, Reichstag Building Burned Down 72

Bolshevik Revolutionary Signal 73

Many Communist Leaders Arrested 74

The National News Agency, Berlin, 27th: Tonight, at nearly 9:00 p.m., a fire suddenly broke out in the Reichstag building. The flames were raging, and could be seen from afar in Berlin. Fire brigades from all over the city heard the alarm and rushed to help put out the fire. At this time, rumors spread in Berlin, and the people were very panicked. Some said that fires had broken out simultaneously in four places, and one place was caused by a bomb explosion. Therefore, there is no doubt that this fire was caused by arson by rioters. After an hour and a half of hard work by the fire brigades, the flames were finally suppressed, but the Reichstag building had been burned down, causing incalculable losses. The grand assembly hall was completely burned down, and the large dome of the building, which was once a magnificent sight admired by the masses, has now collapsed due to the intense heat, and a part of it has already collapsed. When the fire subsided slightly, the police immediately searched many places around and arrested a Dutchman. After police interrogation, it was learned that the man's name was Luba, only 24 years old. According to Luba's confession, he acted alone and had no party affiliation. However, according to outside reports, fires broke out simultaneously in no less than twenty places in the city, and there may be a major conspiracy behind it. Therefore, the police are still searching.

The National News Agency, Berlin, 28th: Police are now stationed at various key points in the city, and people are still very panicked. The National Socialist Party's stormtroopers and the Steel Helmet organization have formed emergency police teams to prepare for incidents. According to police investigations, this arson was meticulously planned. Flammable materials and explosives were hidden in four places inside the Reichstag building. The main hall has been completely destroyed, and the audience seats, press rooms, and rest rooms have also been severely damaged. This proves that the perpetrators are not limited to Luba alone, and there must be accomplices. It is expected that the detained communists will be interrogated and the truth will come out. As for the communists' planned uprising plan, it has not been fully released, and the party is also investigating suspected persons. It is expected that there will be more arrests. However, although this conspiracy to start an incident has been completely suppressed, the people in various places are deeply afraid that the communists, out of anger and resentment, will retaliate, so they are quite panicked.

The Berlin Reichstag building is located in Republic Square, very close to Brandenburg Gate. Adjacent to it is the Tiergarten. It was built in 1894 by the famous architect Wallot according to the wishes of the deposed emperor. It is truly a magnificent masterpiece of the previous generation.

Before the Reichstag building caught fire, a fire also broke out in the deposed German Emperor's Palace. The deposed palace is located next to the Lustgarten and is the most magnificent building on Unter den Linden Street in Berlin. When the guards discovered black smoke, they immediately went inside to inspect and found a room with a large amount of flammable material burning. Therefore, they immediately extinguished it, preventing a major disaster. The arrested Dutchman has admitted that he also set the fire in the deposed palace, but insisted that he had no accomplices.

The National News Agency, Berlin, 28th: Yesterday, the cabinet meeting passed the Law on Punishing Treason. Any soldier who commits treasonous acts will be sentenced to life imprisonment or death. Spreading rumors abroad to endanger the country will also be punished. This order can be signed by President von Hindenburg today.

Reuters, Berlin, 28th: Goering, the Prussian Minister of the Interior, issued a public statement on the Reichstag fire, saying that this was the most serious act of violence committed by German Bolsheviks in history. The statement announced that Communist Party members will be arrested within days. It also stated that the recent seizure of the Communist Party headquarters in Berlin revealed a plan that proves that today's fire was a signal for a Bolshevik revolution. After the Reichstag caught fire, the police arrested two people inside, said to be a Dutchman named Luba, who confessed to arson but did not admit to being instructed by anyone. All Communist Party newspapers in Prussia have been banned from publication for four weeks, and Socialist Party newspapers have been banned for two weeks.

Reuters, Berlin, 28th: Goering has ordered the arrest of Communist Party members, numbering nearly 100. This morning, police confiscated all Communist Party and Socialist Party newspapers, leaflets, and periodicals in Berlin and banned their continuation. Police searched the Forward newspaper office and took away two truckloads of confiscated newspapers. Reuters, Berlin, 28th: The authorities have arrested 80 communists, including 38 leaders. The Communist Party's legal advisor, Li Deng, is also among them. It is heard that Luba is well-known in American police circles. He is a member of the Dutch Communist Party and obtained a passport in 1931 to travel to Russia. Nothing has been heard of him since then, until last night, when his name became known. The damage to the Reichstag caused by the fire will take several months to repair, so there is no venue available for the time being. The Prussian parliament hall is too small, and the new parliament may be held in another town in Germany in the future.

Reuters, Berlin, 28th: According to Goering, the Communist Party is determined to continue to carry out terrorist acts and will dress in police, Steel Helmet organization, and National Socialist Party uniforms to do so. The authorities also announced that Sunday's general election will proceed as usual without any hindrance. 130 people have been arrested in Berlin, and 140 people have been arrested in Hanover.

Colombia and Peru Cease Fire 75

The National News Agency, Geneva, 27th: The governments of Colombia and Peru have notified the League of Nations that they will cease hostilities and order their troops to remain in their current positions, pending detailed discussions by the League of Nations on who should own Leticia and its adjacent areas. According to telegrams received here, the two governments have ordered their commanders to cease all military activities and await further orders. The financial difficulties of the two countries, coupled with the pressure exerted by neutral countries, finally forced the two governments to reluctantly comply with the advice of other countries to stop their undeclared war and abide by the current peace treaties. The League of Nations will hold a meeting soon to discuss Peru's request to amend the Solomon-Lozano Treaties and return the port of Leticia to Peru. The reason given is that since the signing of the treaty ceding the port of Leticia to Colombia, the Colombian government has not fulfilled other provisions in the treaty.

Havas, Geneva, 28th: The League of Nations Council has established a three-person committee to handle the dispute between Colombia and Peru. After meeting last night, the committee submitted clear recommendations to Peru, the conditions of which are more resolute than previous recommendations. The committee insists on sending a temporary administrative committee to Leticia, composed of one person from Brazil, one person from the United States, and one person from Switzerland. If a written reply of Peru's approval in principle is received in Geneva, the Council will meet tomorrow.

Conference on Disarmament Agrees Not to Resort to Force 76

Its Scope Limited to Europe

Amendment to the Pact of Paris

Will Arouse Strong Opposition

Reuters, Geneva, 28th – The Drafting Committee of the Conference on Disarmament is currently studying the British proposal for an early declaration stating non-resort to force. Today, it agreed on the following draft declaration: "The governments of [blank countries], in order to enhance the spirit of mutual trust among European nations and to promote the cause of disarmament, and being deeply concerned about a joint declaration explicitly prohibiting the use of force in the context of the Paris Pact, solemnly declare that under no circumstances shall they resort to force against one another as an instrument of national policy." This draft will be discussed by the Political Committee at a later date and is expected to arouse strong opposition, especially from Soviet Russia. It is also reported that Denmark, Norway, and Sweden will also consider this declaration insufficient, as they understand it to be an amendment to the Paris Pact, attached with all the reservations contained in the Paris Pact. It is further reported that difficulties have arisen in the Aviation Committee. Germany insists on being certain that military aircraft can be abolished before it is willing to discuss the internationalization of civil aviation. This morning, representatives from Britain, Germany, and Spain discussed the matter. The German representative refused to attend the meeting and declined to participate in the discussion. The British and Spanish representatives then decided to adjourn the Aviation Committee indefinitely. Germany's obstruction in various levels of the Conference on Disarmament is becoming increasingly forceful, as Germany seeks to obtain a satisfactory solution on the issue of equality in disarmament.

Japanese Stock Market Collapse 77

(Dentsu News Agency, Tokyo, 28th) – The Tokyo stock market has experienced another collapse, with sellers rushing in. New Dong stocks fell by 3.50 yen, closing at 66.90 yen, and ended at 65.50 yen. The reason is due to the current situation.

(China United News Agency, Tokyo, 28th) According to the Japanese Ministry of Finance's bulletin, the estimated foreign trade for sixteen ports this week shows exports of 41,507,000 yen and imports of 56,347,000 yen, totaling 97,854,000 yen. The trade deficit is 14,840,000 yen. Since January, the total trade deficit has reached 126,647,000 yen.

Hoover Prepares to Hand Over Power 78

Farewell Letter to Party Members Emphasizes National Affairs as Paramount

National News Agency, Washington, 27th – President Hoover sent a farewell letter to the Republican National Committee, thanking the Republican Party for bestowing him with high honor, and encouraging the party to support the new government's sound actions that benefit the overall situation, stating that at this time, the interests of the people should be paramount, and wholehearted cooperation should be given, setting aside partisan views for the time being. It is reported that Hoover plans to return to his hometown of Palo Alto on Saturday after leaving office and will likely rest for a year.

National News Agency, Washington, 27th – According to a telegram from New York's Hyde, President-elect Roosevelt's inaugural address will only take eight minutes to complete. Therefore, it is widely believed that Roosevelt will not elaborate on the new government's foreign policy but will leave it to the new Secretary of State, Hull, to announce. However, informed sources here also believe that Hull may not make a general statement either, but will only reveal information from time to time in his talks with various countries and in diplomatic notes. This approach is different from the Republican Party's practice. People here feel deeply disappointed by the news that the inaugural address will be so brief and that Roosevelt only began drafting it today.

Zhu Qinglan Appeals for Donations to Save the Nation 81

Zhu Qinglan's circular telegram reads: (Titles omitted) "Greetings to all. Recently, the enemy has invaded the province of Jehol, advancing relentlessly. In a matter of days, the situation has deteriorated. Fortunately, our officers and soldiers have fought bravely to resist and responded calmly, enabling us to maintain the precarious situation. The terrain of Jehol is strategically important, serving as a base for the recovery of lost territory. Therefore, the survival of the province is critically important, relating to the future of the military and the attention of the international community. In other words, saving Jehol is saving the Northeast, and thus saving the nation. The situation is extremely critical, and a moment's delay could be devastating. However, our comrades in the front lines lack food, supplies, clothing, and footwear. Without a continuous supply, how can they resist for long? Furthermore, the number of refugees in the war zone is increasing daily. Homes are destroyed, and people are dying, with nowhere to live. Qinglan has personally experienced the situation in Jehol and witnessed the suffering firsthand. The state of the nation is such that I am filled with sorrow. I hope that compatriots from all walks of life will share these difficult times and unite to save the nation. I earnestly implore you that any donations of funds be sent to the Shanghai Jing'an Temple Road Local Association or the Northeast Refugee Relief Association at 40 Ningbo Road, Guangzhao Public Hall. Those in the north can send donations to the Beiping Newspaper Street 74 National Government Relief Committee, Beiping Office, or any of the major banks such as the Bank of China, the Jiaotong Bank, the Jin Cheng Bank, the Dalu Bank, and the Salt Bank, which can forward the donations. Qinglan will personally ensure that they are distributed effectively to live up to the good intentions of those who are concerned. Zhu Qinglan bows in respect."

Nanjing Road Business Community Notifies Merchants to Donate to Save the Nation 82

The Nanjing Road Business Federation and the First District Branch of the Municipal Federation, in view of the worsening situation in the Northeast, specially notified their member merchants yesterday to promptly donate to support the front lines. The association's notice is recorded as follows: "The situation in the Northeast is becoming increasingly precarious. If Jehol falls, then Mongolia will inevitably be seized by Japan as well, fulfilling their policy of unifying Manchuria and Mongolia. At the same time, Tianjin and Beiping are in danger and may force our authorities to make deals under duress. Although the soldiers are willing to fight, the overall situation has passed the point where defeat can be turned into victory. If we rely on the help of other countries and create a major war, without first discussing who will win or lose or what the aims of each country are, then our country's land will be turned into a battlefield, and the loss of life and property will be unspeakable. Therefore, the best plan for now is to make a concerted effort, to ensure that the soldiers are used wisely, first to hold the ground and prevent its loss, and then to turn defense into offense, directly attack the puppet state, drive out the invaders, and recover our territory. However, for the soldiers to be able to win, they must rely on sharp weapons as their vanguard and the spirit of the people as their rearguard. Although the Shanghai business community has suffered from the impact of the January 28th Incident, affecting both the economy and business, if we think about the environment after the Northeast is definitively lost and the war is lost, or perhaps even the current situation will not be able to be preserved, then rather than regretting it later, why not follow the example of Xian Gao, who lightly valued wealth to save his country, and Bu Shi, who transported supplies to help the border, so that the front lines can receive our support and boost their morale to frustrate the enemy? Therefore, we dare to implore our members and colleagues to open their purses as soon as possible. The more you give, the better, but even a small amount is still appreciated. As for the collection points and methods of use, we must seek public resolution of good strategies and implement them in order. This association's work has always sought openness, and we hope that you will review and support us to jointly plan to save the nation. This is our notice."

Representatives of Universities and Colleges in Pingjin, Mou Mo, Arrives in Shanghai for Talks 87

Reporting on the war situation at the front line of anti-Japanese efforts

Soliciting donations from all sectors

The Joint Association of Faculty and Staff of National Universities and Colleges in Pingjin previously sent representatives with military supplies to inspect the military appearance on the front lines of Jehol and to reward the anti-Japanese soldiers. After returning to Beiping, they convened a plenary meeting to expand publicity and assist the blood-fighting soldiers. It was decided to send four representatives to different regions to promote the cause throughout the provinces and negotiate unified assistance methods. The second district includes the four provinces of Hebei, Henan, Shanxi, and Shaanxi, and Mr. Liu Shichuan was sent there. The second district includes the four provinces of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi, and Mr. Cai Zengtang was sent there. The fourth district includes the three provinces of Guangdong, Guangxi, and Fujian, and Mr. Jia Chengzhang was sent there. The third district includes the four provinces of Shandong, Anhui, Zhejiang, and Jiangsu, and Mr. Mou Mo is representing. Mr. Mou left Beiping on the 19th and stayed in Jinan and Nanjing for a few days to run around and negotiate with all sectors and openly report on the anti-Japanese situation on the front line. He left Nanjing on the evening of the 26th and arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning. He will contact all parties and is scheduled to host the press this afternoon. The Municipal Bureau of Education is scheduled to convene all principals of secondary schools and above in the city at the Bureau of Education on the 1st to ask him to report. It is reported that Mr. Mou will stay in Shanghai for five or six days before heading to Zhejiang and Anhui for publicity. The Central News Agency reporter visited Mr. Mou the night before last for a long interview. Details are described below.

Situation on the Front Line 88

Since the fall of Shanhaiguan, the people of Pingjin

are in a state of panic and are flocking to all directions to seek refuge. The area around the East Legation Quarter has suddenly seen an increase in wealthy guests, and all major hotels are full, with even those who pre-register. The education community, not knowing the truth, is even more worried about the social unrest and convened a joint meeting of representatives. Representatives from all national universities and colleges in Pingjin attended. At that time, they all advocated sending representatives to the front lines to inspect the actual situation, but the war zone was dangerous, and the representatives would bear heavy responsibility if they encountered misfortune. Therefore, they changed to voluntary registration. Nine people signed up on the spot, but only four remained when they set off. Despite various difficulties, they were still able to reach the front lines. Mr. Mou, who is traveling south this time, is also one of those who personally went to the front lines. The military situation on the front line, according to Mr. Mou, is very exciting, and the morale of the people is particularly strong. People drive their cars to transport supplies for the army and even carry baskets to help the engineers dig trenches. The soldiers on the front lines, though thinly clothed, do not show any sign of shrinking back. Upon hearing the sound of killing the enemy, they become even more excited. However, while the military morale is high, the supply of materials is really lacking. The most important thing is the vehicles for transportation and the cold-proof and bullet-proof helmets. A detailed investigation has been carried out and reported to all sectors for careful consideration for purchase and donation.

Donations from Pingjin 89

After Mr. Mou and others returned to Beiping, they convened a

plenary meeting to discuss assistance methods. On the spot, the entire body voluntarily donated 20% of their salaries, totaling 72,000 yuan. They purchased 36 trucks and steel helmets, gas masks, etc. and transported them to Jehol. At the same time, they reported to all sectors. More than 50 households have moved back from the East Legation Quarter, and the number of hotel guests has gradually decreased. With the people's hearts settled, they collectively planned assistance strategies. In a few days, the banking sector raised 60,000 yuan, the military and political sector raised 50,000 yuan, and the industrial and commercial sector raised 20,000 yuan. However, although the people in the Pingjin area are enthusiastic about donating, the amount is still small. Therefore, it was decided to send representatives to promote the cause throughout the provinces and to negotiate assistance methods. The four representatives all left Beiping on the 19th and went to different places.

Experiences Traveling South 90

Mou Mo was assigned to the four provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, and Shandong for publicity. According to Mr. Mou, when the general meeting made the resolution, he was bedridden due to the hardships of traveling north. After receiving the news, his illness worsened. However, due to the encouragement of friends and the drive of patriotism, he embarked on the journey despite his illness. He left Tianjin on the 19th of last month and arrived in Jinan on the 20th. He stayed for two days, contacting all sectors, and gave a public report at the People's Education Center, which was attended by thousands of people. The presentation lasted for more than two hours, and no one showed signs of fatigue. He left Jinan on the 22nd and arrived in Nanjing on the 23rd. He also reported to and contacted all sectors of the Party and government. All parties gave him a warm welcome and set up a general office at the Nanjing Municipal Party Headquarters. He originally planned to stay in Nanjing for three days, but he delayed it for one day at the request of the People's Education Center. He came to Shanghai this morning. Shanghai is the economic center of the country, and its people's patriotic fervor is no less than that of other places. During the January 28th Incident last year, the rear support was particularly enthusiastic. Therefore, I have great hope for Shanghai and wish to stay for a few days to talk in detail with all sectors. After arriving in Shanghai today, I immediately visited Mayor Wu and Director Pan, who both gave me enthusiastic instructions. It has now been decided to host the press at noon tomorrow (28th). Director Pan also promised to convene all principals of secondary schools and above in the city at the Bureau of Education on Thursday for me to report. As for the Northeast Association and the Local Association, I will also contact them. After completing these tasks, I will immediately go to Hangzhou, then to Anhui, and return to Beiping.

Municipal Government Approves Preparation for Land Value Tax Collection 91

And Orders the Finance and Land Bureaus to Proceed Swiftly

The city government, after submitting a request to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Interior for approval to collect land value tax in this city, immediately ordered the Finance and Land Bureaus to jointly review the collection methods. The two bureaus have now held several consultations and decided to first organize the Shanghai Preparatory Joint Committee for Provisional Land Tax Collection to begin preparations so that collection can begin as soon as possible. Yesterday, they also submitted the Preparatory Committee's regulations to the city government. The city government considered that the proposed plan was appropriate and approved it for record. It immediately ordered them to proceed quickly. The two bureaus' submissions and regulations are recorded below.

Submission 92

Submission Regarding Application: Regarding the case of provisional land value tax collection in this city, previously approved by the City Government Secretariat's telegrams No. 831 and No. 839, copies of the telegrams from the Ministry of Interior and Ministry of Finance were sent successively to reply to the Shanghai land value tax case. After repeated consultations, it was decided to temporarily implement the tax. You are requested to review, etc. After repeated consultations, this bureau and others believed that since this case has been approved for implementation, preparations should be made quickly so that collection can begin as soon as possible. However, there are related relationships between the two bureaus in terms of procedures. In order to expedite the handling of affairs and facilitate contact, it is proposed to establish a joint committee between the two bureaus to jointly discuss and proceed, to avoid separation. The regulations of the Shanghai Preparatory Joint Committee for Provisional Land Tax Collection have now been drafted. This submission is made together with the regulations, requesting review and approval for record and instructions to comply with. It is truly for the public benefit. In addition, this submission was drafted primarily by the Land Bureau, and it includes a joint signature but no seal, and it is stated for the record. Respectfully submitted.

Regulations 93

Shanghai Preparatory Joint Committee for Provisional Land Value Tax Regulations: Article 1: The Shanghai Preparatory Joint Committee for Provisional Land Tax Collection is specially established for quick handling and easy contact. Article 2: The Committee shall have seven members, and the section chiefs of the Finance and Land Bureaus shall serve as members. Article 3: The Chairman of the Committee shall be elected by the members. Article 4: The Committee shall hold a regular meeting every Thursday at 3:00 PM. When necessary, the Chairman may convene it at any time. Article 5: When necessary, the Committee may appoint relevant section members to attend meetings for discussion. Article 6: The Committee is attached to the Land Bureau. Article 7: These regulations shall be submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and record before implementation.

However, our tens of thousands of brave soldiers who have been fighting for years, trekking thousands of miles, risking their lives, and sacrificing themselves for the country have no pay and no clothes to cover their bodies. Moreover, their horses have no saddles, and the people are barefoot and unkempt, like prisoners. As the commander, how can Wen drive them to fight? I also cannot bear to drive them to fight. Those who came before have not completely changed their clothes, and those who come later are likely to be even more discouraged. Therefore, I specially send this telegram to your association, earnestly requesting further assistance, such as military uniforms, underwear, socks, boots, cotton blankets, horse saddles, large and small radios, telephone equipment, and trucks. If we have supplements, we can boost the morale of the soldiers and display the power of our army, annihilating those ugly captives and returning our territory. This will not only be deeply engraved in the hearts of all soldiers in the enemy army, but it is also truly reliant on the future of the country. Deng Wen, Commander of the First Army of Heilongjiang, bows."

Rice Merchants Strike over Transportation Disputes Heard Yesterday 100

According to the Ta Kung Press, news from all parties regarding the rice merchants' strike over transportation disputes is as follows:

Rice Shops to Suspend Business Today 101

The Doumi Guild in the North and South Cities, due to the lack of regulation of commissions and frequent disruptions by fellow traders, has had a negative impact on the business. In order to strictly rectify the situation, the guild organized a small group to draft punishment regulations. Yesterday, the guild notified all businesses in the North and South Cities that it would be closed for one day starting this morning, and it would convene a general meeting of managers and brokers at 2:00 PM this afternoon to discuss rectification methods.

Party and Government to Mediate Today 102

Regarding the strike by rice transporters, the Party and government authorities have scheduled a formal mediation at 10:00 AM today. Notification letters were issued separately yesterday afternoon. Because of the strike by rice transporters who are opposed to remeasuring, the shipowners have launched a large-scale attack. The Rice Measurers' Union has submitted a request to the Party and government authorities for relief and also requested permission to independently organize a Rice Measurers' Management Committee to exercise fair authority. International Trade Bureau Compiles and Prints the China Industry Journal 113

Jiangsu Province Has Already Been Published

The Ministry of Industry's National Trade Bureau has compiled a national industry journal, starting with Jiangsu Province, as reported in previous news. It is now learned that the China Industry Journal of Jiangsu Province has been compiled, printed, and published today. The book contains two million words, totaling over two thousand four hundred pages. This magnificent work is rich in materials and exquisitely bound. The reporter believes that this matter is still an innovation in our country, and the compilation of the industry journal is unprecedented and of great importance. Therefore, I went to the International Trade Bureau to inquire about everything and met with Mr. Hou Houpei, the Director of Investigation in charge of this matter. Mr. Hou kindly informed me of various details. This investigation, thanks to the enthusiasm and supervision of Minister Chen and Director He, proceeded without delay during the implementation period, so it was able to complete this heavy and massive work in a very short time. There are several points that urgently need to be explained at the time of publication: (1) The purpose of this investigation is entirely to promote industry, so the selection of materials also focuses on the production and sales aspects, so its purpose is also mainly for general reference, rather than for professional research. (2) Although the investigation materials are novel, they seem to only be useful for people outside the industry to refer to, and the reference materials for people in the industry may feel insufficient. (3) Economic conditions are constantly changing, and the industries in Jiangsu are too numerous to mention, and the various industries that have not been added will be added in the future using the addendum method. (4) The time period for the investigation and collection of materials is within three months, from September to November of the 21st year of the Republic of China, which is quite unified. Comparative observation can also be in line with the principles. However, the investigation and compilation periods are very short, but colleagues have strictly reviewed the data and proofreading, and have tried their best to ask experts to proofread and correct them, and dare not be negligent. As for errors, it is inevitable, and I hope that all sectors will give instructions, etc.

Three New Buoys Added in the Huangpu River 116

The Continental Daily reported that the port authorities announced yesterday (the 27th) that three new buoys have been added to the Huangpu River, all of which can be completed and available for use tomorrow (the 1st). Their locations are all near the Xigou downstream of the Mei Zi Shipyard, providing mooring positions for four ships. Two of them can accommodate the largest imported ships, and the remaining two can accommodate medium-sized ocean-going ships. In the future, there will be 55 mooring positions with buoys in the Huangpu River, all under the management of the Customs, of which three are dedicated to Customs patrol boats, two are dedicated to fishing boats, and three are dedicated to fishing vessels. The remaining 47 are for ocean-going and coastal ships to anchor. In addition, there are five mooring positions owned by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and seven owned by the Jiangnan Shipyard. At present, the largest imported ships can reach a draft of 32 feet, but such giant ships are rarely imported. The new buoys can accommodate giant ships with a draft of 30 feet. According to reports, the current buoys in the Huangpu River were equipped by the Customs in early 1921. Before that, they were only privately owned. Subsequently, in 1926, the positions of the buoys were rearranged, and in 1928, the number of buoys was increased to facilitate navigation. Recently, three more buoys have been added, and at the same time, the old buoys have been replaced with new-style buoys, and 12 have been replaced to date.

Stamp Duty Issue on Car Signature Slips 117

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Strives to Waive the Fine

The cases of the Xiangsheng and Lili car companies in this city having their time signature slips confiscated by the stamp duty inspection office and ordered to be fined have caused resentment among merchants and citizens who believe the fines are inappropriate. The details are recorded as follows.

Letter from the Car Industry to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

The Car Industry Association's letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce states:

"Respectfully, regarding the matter of the time counting signature slips used by the industry, on the 10th and 15th of this month, the Concession Cigarette Inspection Office, together with the police patrol team, confiscated the time counting signature slips, etc. On the 14th, we sent a letter to your chamber to forward to the Jiangsu Stamp Duty Bureau to cancel the stamp duty on the signature slips and to quickly return the confiscated slips to maintain business, etc. However, more than ten days have passed, and they have not been returned. Unexpectedly, at 9:00 a.m. today, police lawyer Ru Bao Yi filed a lawsuit for violation of regulations. The Ninth Court ruled that Lili Car Company should be fined 1,000 yuan, Xiangsheng Car Company should be fined 1,000 yuan, and Xinzha Car Company should be fined 300 yuan, and that all signature slips used by the industry in the future must be fully stamped, completely disregarding the instructions issued by the Shanghai Special Zone Office of the Jiangsu Tobacco and Alcohol Stamp Duty Bureau on June 9, 1931, which stated that stamping was exempt. The police lawyer's one-sided statement was accepted, and the ruling was made. Such a discrepancy in tax policy is unbearable for merchants and citizens. The industry is trembling in this situation. Moreover, the industry follows the regulations of the Ministry of Industry to prepare time counting signature slips, which do not resemble receipt of money in any way, and there is no regulation or item that requires full stamping. If this precedent is set, the Datang Car Company will need to stamp about 10,000 yuan or more each year, and small car companies will also need to stamp several thousand yuan. At a time when businesses are losing money, how can they bear such a heavy burden? The industry will inevitably close down one after another. If they do not follow the judgment and stamp receipts, they will inevitably be inspected and fined one by one. There are many people in the industry, and their hearts are not united. If they become indignant and an accident occurs, it may cause unrest in society. Based on these facts, the Association dares to send a letter to your chamber, urging you to telegraph the Ministry of Finance and order the Taxation Department to stop inspecting the industry's signature slips. This matter concerns the survival of the industry, so a corresponding letter is sent, hoping that you will investigate and handle it accordingly."

Municipal Chamber of Commerce's Telegram to the Ministry of Finance 118

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce's telegram to the Ministry of Finance states: "To the Nanjing Ministry of Finance: The main point of this case is that the signature slip is not a similar item in the stamp duty regulations that can be compared for stamping. Therefore, on June 1, 1931, the Special Zone Office had instructions not to stamp signature slips that were not for receipt of money. Although the Special Zone Office's handling of violation cases has been transferred to the Cigarette Consolidated Tax Inspection Office, how can the previous approved exemption be completely erased due to changes in jurisdiction? If government offices do not follow the established regulations, what can merchants and citizens do? These circumstances were reported to you in a telegram on the 15th of this month. Based on the previous situation, in addition to the three cases that have been judged and fined, which will be handled separately by the parties concerned according to law, it is proposed that your ministry order the Consolidated Tax Department to maintain the original case of exempting signature counting slips from stamp duty, so as to prevent the Inspection Office from making arbitrary and unreasonable demands. This is for the public benefit. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce humbly requests."

Our municipal government is working hard on construction and seeking the revitalization of the entire city. It must not regard Laiyi Ferry Town as being outside the sphere of influence. The matter is urgent, and we have no choice but to submit another letter to your association, requesting that you quickly forward it to the Municipal Government, taking into account the public interest, and clearly ordering that the ferry crossing be open forever. The 100,000 residents of our entire town pledge to be the government's backing and to deal with those who only care about their own selfish interests.' The letter has been received by the Association. Regarding this matter, according to the letter from the branch office, we submitted a letter to your government on the 6th of this month, requesting that the Hongsheng Company not block the public wharf for Chinese merchants. Now, according to the follow-up report, it is not known whether the company has not received the order from your government to stop the blocking, or whether it intends to show contempt.
